Australia\u2019s best-value fruit and veg for April", "standfirst": "<p>Broccoli and cauliflower headline this month\u2019s market buys, while apples and pears herald the start of autumnal fruit</p><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/newsletters/2019/oct/18/saved-for-later-sign-up-for-guardian-australias-culture-and-lifestyle-email?CMP=cvau_sfl\">Get our weekend culture and lifestyle email</a></li></ul>", "trailText": "Broccoli and cauliflower headline this month\u2019s market buys, while apples and pears herald the start of autumnal fruit", "byline": "Maddie Thomas", "main": "<figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"776c065bd42f1c704d29308a03bfd11b5bc0e888\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/776c065bd42f1c704d29308a03bfd11b5bc0e888/43_374_4569_3046/1000.jpg\" alt=\"A frying pan with broccoli and cauliflower in natural sunlight\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Brassicas such as broccoli and cauliflower are your best vegetable buys for April.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Jelena Matvejeva/Getty Images/EyeEm</span> </figcaption> </figure>", "body": "<p>April guarantees a plentiful supply of chocolate eggs, hot cross buns \u2026 and broccoli. There are plenty of fresh, affordable vegetables this month, and the green brassica stands out for all the right reasons.</p> <p>\u201c[Broccoli] is cheap, affordable and something that most families enjoy,\u201d says George Vasilevski, the owner of Yarraville Square Fresh Market in Melbourne.</p> <p>\u201cYou can find a rougher-grade broccoli, which doesn\u2019t look as pretty but is just as fresh, for as little as $2 a kilo but you shouldn\u2019t be paying more than $6 a kilo for the best.\u201d In supermarkets it can be found for about $4 a kilo.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"0be805ec037a6b5f42f4359ebb2f010998c046f8\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/0be805ec037a6b5f42f4359ebb2f010998c046f8/0_0_5760_3840/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Oval black oven dish with broccoli and cheese gratin\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Alex Bluett\u2019s broccoli and blue\u2011cheese bake, one of his four recipes with the roasted vegetable.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Yuki Sugiura/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Roasting is one of the best ways to cook broccoli \u2013 the high heat gives a complex, nutty savouriness to the florets and stalks. With one large batch of roasted broccoli, the chef Alex Bluett has created <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2015/may/30/broccoli-recipe-four-different-meals-alex-bluett\">four recipes</a>: a salad, a blue-cheese gratin, a soup and a toastie.</p> <p>If you need to be broc-convinced, the vegetable goes (almost) incognito in Yotam Ottolenghi\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2019/may/04/yotam-ottolenghi-broccoli-recipes-fried-pickled-rocket-pasta-mushroom-ketchup\">orecchiette with broccoli and rocket</a>. For the converted, Rachel Roddy\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2015/nov/03/twice-cooked-broccoli-repassati-recipe-rachel-roddy\">broccoli ripassati</a> tossed through casarecce is the green pasta of choice.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"c90a2535aa4123f96453024d7681476b209ab9dd\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/c90a2535aa4123f96453024d7681476b209ab9dd/0_0_3731_4384/851.jpg\" alt=\"A round pan with short pasta, broccoli and rocket.\" width=\"851\" height=\"1000\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Yotam Ottolenghi\u2019s orecchiette with broccoli and rocket.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Louise Hagger/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Elsewhere in the brassica family, Vasilevski says there are plenty of bargain buys this month.</p> <p>Cauliflowers are back, and a steal at about $2.50 to $3 each. Get ahead with Felicity Cloake\u2019s guide to cooking the <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/wordofmouth/2017/apr/13/how-to-cook-perfect-roasted-cauliflower-felicity-cloake\">perfect whole-roasted cauliflower</a> before spinning off with <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2021/dec/19/nigel-slater-recipes-for-roast-cauliflower-plus-festive-chocolate-treats\">Nigel Slater\u2019s roasted cauliflower with lemon harissa sauce</a> or <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/dec/03/meera-sodha-vegan-recipe-whole-roast-cauliflower-nut-pilaf\">Meera Sodha\u2019s cumin-and-chilli-spiced number with pilaf</a>. And let this be the season for <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/jan/30/one-pound-cauliflower-pasta-tacos-recipes-miguel-barclay\">cauliflower tacos</a>.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"d7b3c53ad0da791c50fc73e4585265efd8699024\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/d7b3c53ad0da791c50fc73e4585265efd8699024/1815_1763_4710_3140/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Roast cauliflower with pilaf on a gold-coloured plate\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Meera Sodha\u2019s whole roast cauliflower and nut pilaf.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Laura Edwards/The Guardian. Food and prop styling: Kitty Coles. Food assistant: El Kemp</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Kale is fresh and crisp at about $4.50 a bunch; a bunch of silverbeet will set you back about $5.50. Half savoy cabbages remain steady at about $3 each in supermarkets, while whole womboks can be found at $4.90 each and are destined for your next homemade <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2020/may/13/how-to-make-kimchi-recipe-felicity-cloake-masterclass\">kimchi</a>.</p> <h2>Keen for zucchinis</h2> <p> April\u2019s zucchinis are gourd\u2019s gifts.</p> <p>Vasilevski calls them \u201cgreat value and very versatile\u201d and is selling them at $2 to $6 a kilo, depending on quality. In supermarkets, they are about $4.50 a kilo.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"b78bc8932079c5f1c5edb43f3326b8db3c53025b\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/b78bc8932079c5f1c5edb43f3326b8db3c53025b/0_0_4877_4222/1000.jpg\" alt=\"A spread of dishes including zucchini moussaka, dolma and koftas\" width=\"1000\" height=\"866\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Aleksandar Taralezhkov\u2019s zucchini moussaka (far left), dolma (top) and koftas (bottom).</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Issy Croker/The Guardian. Food and prop styling: Kitty Coles. Food assistant: Susanna Unsworth</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Mattie Taiano\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/26/courgette-creme-fraiche-and-pecorino-lasagne-recipe-by-mattie-taiano\">zucchini lasagne</a> is meat-free; Alice Zaslavsky\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2022/nov/17/good-gourd-how-to-make-the-most-of-zucchini-season-from-fritters-to-zoodles-recipe\">zucchini fritters</a> are gluten-free, dairy-free, egg-free and nut-free; while Aleksandar Taralezhkov has created a zucchini multiverse with Bulgarian <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/jul/29/summer-courgette-recipes-dolma-kofta-moussaka-aleksandar-taralezhkov\">dolma, moussaka and koftas</a>. </p> <aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail\"> <p> <span>Related: </span><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/21/australian-autumn-recipes-10-yotam-ottolenghi-recipes-to-suit-the-season\">Australian autumn recipes: 10 Yotam Ottolenghi recipes to suit the season</a> </p> </aside>  <p>At the Greener Grocer in Maroubra in Sydney\u2019s east, its manager, Adam Balloot, says April is also the time to watch for grey zucchinis (often sold as Lebanese zucchinis). They are so named for their grey-coloured seeds and have a slightly sweeter flavour than green zucchinis.</p> <p>Red and green capsicums are abundant and can be found for $7 to $8 a kilo in supermarkets. Yellow capsicums, the sweetest of the lot, are about $12 to $13 a kilo. They\u2019re pricier because they have spent more time on the vine before harvesting. If your capsicums have spent a little too long lingering in the fridge, give them a second chance at life with <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2020/aug/17/rachel-roddy-recipe-peppers-and-potatoes\">Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum and potatoes</a>.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"09feeb33f629eb142a039c245179a740189ef73c\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/09feeb33f629eb142a039c245179a740189ef73c/0_0_4000_3000/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Composite image of sauteed red capsicums, lettuce and potatoes in a frying pan, and in a serving bowl\" width=\"1000\" height=\"750\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum with potatoes.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Rachel Roddy/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Also in stable supply are Asian greens, eggplant, corn and fennel.<br><br>After a late-summer glut, it\u2019s wise to leave tomatoes off your shopping list. \u201cAbout a month ago, we were selling 1kg bags for $2.50,\u201d Balloot says. \u201cToday, we have a 1kg bag for $4.\u201d</p> <p>In supermarkets, most varieties have risen to $7 or $8 a kilo for loose tomatoes. \u201cIf you can get your hands on a prepacked one, that\u2019s going to be a better deal right now,\u201d Balloot says.<br><br>He says avocados are \u201cstill a bit iffy\u201d and, while prices are slowly going down each week, the much-loved Hass variety is not expected to return soon. Which means now is the time to <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/14/learning-to-love-shepard-avocados-unlike-the-hass-this-is-smooth-rich-and-unthreatening\">embrace Shepards</a>.</p> <h2>A is for April, autumn and apples</h2> <p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/02/watermelons-hit-the-sweet-spot-australias-best-value-fruit-and-veg-for-march\">Last month\u2019s picks</a> \u2013 grapes and watermelons \u2013 remain at a good price but April is the apple\u2019s time to shine. </p> <p>Royal Galas are cheapest at about $3.90 a kilo, with Jazz, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2021/may/12/i-want-kanzi-a-new-australian-apple-variety-comes-into-its-own\">Kanzi</a> and Fuji apples at about $5 a kilo. The latter variety is good for baking into these <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2019/oct/26/toffee-apple-and-crumble-four-recipes-for-easy-apple-bakes\">cakes, tarts and apple crumble muffins</a>.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"359331d2f1f4fd9e26c83ef59ebe5d77818ea119\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/359331d2f1f4fd9e26c83ef59ebe5d77818ea119/0_0_3537_3537/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Four apple crumble muffins on a grey plate\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1000\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Part apple, part crumble, all muffin: James Rich\u2019s apple crumble muffins.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Ola O Smit/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>\u201cThe most popular are Pink Ladies, but they\u2019re one of the last apples to come in. They\u2019re about a month away,\u201d Vasilevski says. <br><br>Pears have also started falling in price, from about $2.90 (on special) to $5 a kilo. Combine the two autumnal fruits in Tamal Ray\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2020/sep/19/tamal-ray-recipe-apple-and-pear-tart\">apple and pear tart</a> with a rum and star anise glaze. The recipe calls for conference pears, which can be hard to find in Australia \u2013 substitute with William Bartlett or beurre bosc.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"f75c1bc8fce398a17ee9452bb26631e4ed332085\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/f75c1bc8fce398a17ee9452bb26631e4ed332085/355_1323_5327_6140/868.jpg\" alt=\"Square slice of apple and pear tart drizzled with cream\" width=\"868\" height=\"1000\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Tamal Ray\u2019s apple and pear tart with a rum and star anise glaze.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Laura Edwards/The Guardian. Food styling: Benjamina Ebuehi. Prop styling: Anna Wilkins. Food assistant: Kristine Jakobsson</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Autumn also brings persimmons. At about $3 each, they will come down in price as supply comes in, albeit for a short season. Some prefer the jammy, astringent, teardrop-shaped variety; others prefer the firm Fuyu specimens, which work well in <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/apr/28/persimmons-101-from-crunchy-to-jelly-soft-the-best-ways-to-eat-the-misunderstood-fruit\">Alanna Sapwell\u2019s persimmon tarte tatin</a>.</p> <h2>High on local citrus supply</h2> <aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail\"> <p> <span>Related: </span><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/apr/28/persimmons-101-from-crunchy-to-jelly-soft-the-best-ways-to-eat-the-misunderstood-fruit\">Give persimmon a chance: five ways to eat the misunderstood fruit from salad to Alanna Sapwell\u2019s tarte tartin</a> </p> </aside>  <p>While vegetable supply and prices will largely remain steady, Neha Thaker, owner of <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/vinceandcharlies/\">Vince and Charlie\u2019s Fruit Market</a> in Ferny Hills, north-west of Brisbane, says fruit is not as consistent in cooler months.</p> <p>\u201cThe new season fruit is at peak prices at the moment,\u201d she says. \u201cMandarins are coming \u2013 they\u2019re beautiful - but they\u2019re quite high in price still, like $10 a kilo.\u201d</p> <p>Local citrus will enter the market towards the end of April, bringing an end to imported navel oranges. They\u2019re now in supermarkets for $6 or $7 a kilo but soon customers will find premium-quality oranges for about $5 a kilo or less. We have this <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2017/jan/14/orange-upside-down-cake-date-salad-recipe-claire-ptak-baking-the-seasons\">upside-down orange cake</a> bookmarked, just in case.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"e8d7d5e27f3c4e6c27000771225be7bb7a4d1532\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/e8d7d5e27f3c4e6c27000771225be7bb7a4d1532/0_311_3840_2560/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Upside-down cake decorated with orange slices\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Claire Ptak\u2019s orange, ginger and rye upside-down cake.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Kristin Perers/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>For now, berries, \u201cone of the most expensive fruits\u201d, are unlikely to come down in price and mangoes are well and truly gone.</p> <p>Keep the summer dream alive with good stone fruit \u2013 the last of the season \u2013 which to Thaker\u2019s surprise, are still good quality.</p> <p>\u201cUsually by this time, they\u2019re going black inside and rotting \u2026 I think customers should make the most of it.\u201d</p> <p><em><strong>Buy:</strong></em> <br>Apples<br>Asian greens<br>Bananas: stable "2023-04-04T00:55:00Z", "productionOffice": "AUS", "publication": "theguardian.com", "shortUrl": "https://www.theguardian.com/p/nkgkz", "shouldHideAdverts": "false", "showInRelatedContent": "true", "thumbnail": "https://media.guim.co.uk/776c065bd42f1c704d29308a03bfd11b5bc0e888/0_421_4611_2767/500.jpg", "legallySensitive": "false", "lang": "en", "isLive": "true", "bodyText": "April guarantees a plentiful supply of chocolate eggs, hot cross buns \u2026 and broccoli. There are plenty of fresh, affordable vegetables this month, and the green brassica stands out for all the right reasons. \u201c[Broccoli] is cheap, affordable and something that most families enjoy,\u201d says George Vasilevski, the owner of Yarraville Square Fresh Market in Melbourne. \u201cYou can find a rougher-grade broccoli, which doesn\u2019t look as pretty but is just as fresh, for as little as $2 a kilo but you shouldn\u2019t be paying more than $6 a kilo for the best.\u201d In supermarkets it can be found for about $4 a kilo. Roasting is one of the best ways to cook broccoli \u2013 the high heat gives a complex, nutty savouriness to the florets and stalks. With one large batch of roasted broccoli, the chef Alex Bluett has created four recipes: a salad, a blue-cheese gratin, a soup and a toastie. If you need to be broc-convinced, the vegetable goes (almost) incognito in Yotam Ottolenghi\u2019s orecchiette with broccoli and rocket. For the converted, Rachel Roddy\u2019s broccoli ripassati tossed through casarecce is the green pasta of choice. Elsewhere in the brassica family, Vasilevski says there are plenty of bargain buys this month. Cauliflowers are back, and a steal at about $2.50 to $3 each. Get ahead with Felicity Cloake\u2019s guide to cooking the perfect whole-roasted cauliflower before spinning off with Nigel Slater\u2019s roasted cauliflower with lemon harissa sauce or Meera Sodha\u2019s cumin-and-chilli-spiced number with pilaf. And let this be the season for cauliflower tacos. Kale is fresh and crisp at about $4.50 a bunch; a bunch of silverbeet will set you back about $5.50. Half savoy cabbages remain steady at about $3 each in supermarkets, while whole womboks can be found at $4.90 each and are destined for your next homemade kimchi. Keen for zucchinis April\u2019s zucchinis are gourd\u2019s gifts. Vasilevski calls them \u201cgreat value and very versatile\u201d and is selling them at $2 to $6 a kilo, depending on quality. In supermarkets, they are about $4.50 a kilo. Mattie Taiano\u2019s zucchini lasagne is meat-free; Alice Zaslavsky\u2019s zucchini fritters are gluten-free, dairy-free, egg-free and nut-free; while Aleksandar Taralezhkov has created a zucchini multiverse with Bulgarian dolma, moussaka and koftas. At the Greener Grocer in Maroubra in Sydney\u2019s east, its manager, Adam Balloot, says April is also the time to watch for grey zucchinis (often sold as Lebanese zucchinis). They are so named for their grey-coloured seeds and have a slightly sweeter flavour than green zucchinis. Red and green capsicums are abundant and can be found for $7 to $8 a kilo in supermarkets. Yellow capsicums, the sweetest of the lot, are about $12 to $13 a kilo. They\u2019re pricier because they have spent more time on the vine before harvesting. If your capsicums have spent a little too long lingering in the fridge, give them a second chance at life with Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum and potatoes. Also in stable supply are Asian greens, eggplant, corn and fennel. After a late-summer glut, it\u2019s wise to leave tomatoes off your shopping list. \u201cAbout a month ago, we were selling 1kg bags for $2.50,\u201d Balloot says. \u201cToday, we have a 1kg bag for $4.\u201d In supermarkets, most varieties have risen to $7 or $8 a kilo for loose tomatoes. \u201cIf you can get your hands on a prepacked one, that\u2019s going to be a better deal right now,\u201d Balloot says. He says avocados are \u201cstill a bit iffy\u201d and, while prices are slowly going down each week, the much-loved Hass variety is not expected to return soon. Which means now is the time to embrace Shepards. A is for April, autumn and apples Last month\u2019s picks \u2013 grapes and watermelons \u2013 remain at a good price but April is the apple\u2019s time to shine. Royal Galas are cheapest at about $3.90 a kilo, with Jazz, Kanzi and Fuji apples at about $5 a kilo. The latter variety is good for baking into these cakes, tarts and apple crumble muffins. \u201cThe most popular are Pink Ladies, but they\u2019re one of the last apples to come in. They\u2019re about a month away,\u201d Vasilevski says. Pears have also started falling in price, from about $2.90 (on special) to $5 a kilo. Combine the two autumnal fruits in Tamal Ray\u2019s apple and pear tart with a rum and star anise glaze. The recipe calls for conference pears, which can be hard to find in Australia \u2013 substitute with William Bartlett or beurre bosc. Autumn also brings persimmons. At about $3 each, they will come down in price as supply comes in, albeit for a short season. Some prefer the jammy, astringent, teardrop-shaped variety; others prefer the firm Fuyu specimens, which work well in Alanna Sapwell\u2019s persimmon tarte tatin. High on local citrus supply While vegetable supply and prices will largely remain steady, Neha Thaker, owner of Vince and Charlie\u2019s Fruit Market in Ferny Hills, north-west of Brisbane, says fruit is not as consistent in cooler months. \u201cThe new season fruit is at peak prices at the moment,\u201d she says. \u201cMandarins are coming \u2013 they\u2019re beautiful - but they\u2019re quite high in price still, like $10 a kilo.\u201d Local citrus will enter the market towards the end of April, bringing an end to imported navel oranges. They\u2019re now in supermarkets for $6 or $7 a kilo but soon customers will find premium-quality oranges for about $5 a kilo or less. We have this upside-down orange cake bookmarked, just in case. For now, berries, \u201cone of the most expensive fruits\u201d, are unlikely to come down in price and mangoes are well and truly gone. Keep the summer dream alive with good stone fruit \u2013 the last of the season \u2013 which to Thaker\u2019s surprise, are still good quality. \u201cUsually by this time, they\u2019re going black inside and rotting \u2026 I think customers should make the most of it.\u201d Buy: Apples Asian greens Bananas: stable year-round Broccoli Broccolini Cauliflower Cabbage Corn Eggplant Fennel Grapes In supermarkets, they are about $4.50 a kilo.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"b78bc8932079c5f1c5edb43f3326b8db3c53025b\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/b78bc8932079c5f1c5edb43f3326b8db3c53025b/0_0_4877_4222/1000.jpg\" alt=\"A spread of dishes including zucchini moussaka, dolma and koftas\" width=\"1000\" height=\"866\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Aleksandar Taralezhkov\u2019s zucchini moussaka (far left), dolma (top) and koftas (bottom).</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Issy Croker/The Guardian. Food and prop styling: Kitty Coles. Food assistant: Susanna Unsworth</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Mattie Taiano\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/26/courgette-creme-fraiche-and-pecorino-lasagne-recipe-by-mattie-taiano\">zucchini lasagne</a> is meat-free; Alice Zaslavsky\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2022/nov/17/good-gourd-how-to-make-the-most-of-zucchini-season-from-fritters-to-zoodles-recipe\">zucchini fritters</a> are gluten-free, dairy-free, egg-free and nut-free; while Aleksandar Taralezhkov has created a zucchini multiverse with Bulgarian <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/jul/29/summer-courgette-recipes-dolma-kofta-moussaka-aleksandar-taralezhkov\">dolma, moussaka and koftas</a>. </p> <aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail\"> <p> <span>Related: </span><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/21/australian-autumn-recipes-10-yotam-ottolenghi-recipes-to-suit-the-season\">Australian autumn recipes: 10 Yotam Ottolenghi recipes to suit the season</a> </p> </aside>  <p>At the Greener Grocer in Maroubra in Sydney\u2019s east, its manager, Adam Balloot, says April is also the time to watch for grey zucchinis (often sold as Lebanese zucchinis). They are so named for their grey-coloured seeds and have a slightly sweeter flavour than green zucchinis.</p> <p>Red and green capsicums are abundant and can be found for $7 to $8 a kilo in supermarkets. Yellow capsicums, the sweetest of the lot, are about $12 to $13 a kilo. They\u2019re pricier because they have spent more time on the vine before harvesting. If your capsicums have spent a little too long lingering in the fridge, give them a second chance at life with <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2020/aug/17/rachel-roddy-recipe-peppers-and-potatoes\">Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum and potatoes</a>.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"09feeb33f629eb142a039c245179a740189ef73c\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/09feeb33f629eb142a039c245179a740189ef73c/0_0_4000_3000/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Composite image of sauteed red capsicums, lettuce and potatoes in a frying pan, and in a serving bowl\" width=\"1000\" height=\"750\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum with potatoes.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Rachel Roddy/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Also in stable supply are Asian greens, eggplant, corn and fennel.<br><br>After a late-summer glut, it\u2019s wise to leave tomatoes off your shopping list. \u201cAbout a month ago, we were selling 1kg bags for $2.50,\u201d Balloot says. \u201cToday, we have a 1kg bag for $4.\u201d</p> <p>In supermarkets, most varieties have risen to $7 or $8 a kilo for loose tomatoes. \u201cIf you can get your hands on a prepacked one, that\u2019s going to be a better deal right now,\u201d Balloot says.<br><br>He says avocados are \u201cstill a bit iffy\u201d and, while prices are slowly going down each week, the much-loved Hass variety is not expected to return soon. Which means now is the time to <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/14/learning-to-love-shepard-avocados-unlike-the-hass-this-is-smooth-rich-and-unthreatening\">embrace Shepards</a>.</p> <h2>A is for April, autumn and apples</h2> <p><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2023/mar/02/watermelons-hit-the-sweet-spot-australias-best-value-fruit-and-veg-for-march\">Last month\u2019s picks</a> \u2013 grapes and watermelons \u2013 remain at a good price but April is the apple\u2019s time to shine. </p> <p>Royal Galas are cheapest at about $3.90 a kilo, with Jazz, <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2021/may/12/i-want-kanzi-a-new-australian-apple-variety-comes-into-its-own\">Kanzi</a> and Fuji apples at about $5 a kilo. The latter variety is good for baking into these <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2019/oct/26/toffee-apple-and-crumble-four-recipes-for-easy-apple-bakes\">cakes, tarts and apple crumble muffins</a>.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"359331d2f1f4fd9e26c83ef59ebe5d77818ea119\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/359331d2f1f4fd9e26c83ef59ebe5d77818ea119/0_0_3537_3537/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Four apple crumble muffins on a grey plate\" width=\"1000\" height=\"1000\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Part apple, part crumble, all muffin: James Rich\u2019s apple crumble muffins.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Ola O Smit/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>\u201cThe most popular are Pink Ladies, but they\u2019re one of the last apples to come in. They\u2019re about a month away,\u201d Vasilevski says. <br><br>Pears have also started falling in price, from about $2.90 (on special) to $5 a kilo. Combine the two autumnal fruits in Tamal Ray\u2019s <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2020/sep/19/tamal-ray-recipe-apple-and-pear-tart\">apple and pear tart</a> with a rum and star anise glaze. The recipe calls for conference pears, which can be hard to find in Australia \u2013 substitute with William Bartlett or beurre bosc.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"f75c1bc8fce398a17ee9452bb26631e4ed332085\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/f75c1bc8fce398a17ee9452bb26631e4ed332085/355_1323_5327_6140/868.jpg\" alt=\"Square slice of apple and pear tart drizzled with cream\" width=\"868\" height=\"1000\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Tamal Ray\u2019s apple and pear tart with a rum and star anise glaze.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Laura Edwards/The Guardian. Food styling: Benjamina Ebuehi. Prop styling: Anna Wilkins. Food assistant: Kristine Jakobsson</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>Autumn also brings persimmons. At about $3 each, they will come down in price as supply comes in, albeit for a short season. Some prefer the jammy, astringent, teardrop-shaped variety; others prefer the firm Fuyu specimens, which work well in <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/apr/28/persimmons-101-from-crunchy-to-jelly-soft-the-best-ways-to-eat-the-misunderstood-fruit\">Alanna Sapwell\u2019s persimmon tarte tatin</a>.</p> <h2>High on local citrus supply</h2> <aside class=\"element element-rich-link element--thumbnail\"> <p> <span>Related: </span><a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/food/2022/apr/28/persimmons-101-from-crunchy-to-jelly-soft-the-best-ways-to-eat-the-misunderstood-fruit\">Give persimmon a chance: five ways to eat the misunderstood fruit from salad to Alanna Sapwell\u2019s tarte tartin</a> </p> </aside>  <p>While vegetable supply and prices will largely remain steady, Neha Thaker, owner of <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/vinceandcharlies/\">Vince and Charlie\u2019s Fruit Market</a> in Ferny Hills, north-west of Brisbane, says fruit is not as consistent in cooler months.</p> <p>\u201cThe new season fruit is at peak prices at the moment,\u201d she says. \u201cMandarins are coming \u2013 they\u2019re beautiful - but they\u2019re quite high in price still, like $10 a kilo.\u201d</p> <p>Local citrus will enter the market towards the end of April, bringing an end to imported navel oranges. They\u2019re now in supermarkets for $6 or $7 a kilo but soon customers will find premium-quality oranges for about $5 a kilo or less. We have this <a href=\"https://www.theguardian.com/lifeandstyle/2017/jan/14/orange-upside-down-cake-date-salad-recipe-claire-ptak-baking-the-seasons\">upside-down orange cake</a> bookmarked, just in case.</p>  <figure class=\"element element-image\" data-media-id=\"e8d7d5e27f3c4e6c27000771225be7bb7a4d1532\"> <img src=\"https://media.guim.co.uk/e8d7d5e27f3c4e6c27000771225be7bb7a4d1532/0_311_3840_2560/1000.jpg\" alt=\"Upside-down cake decorated with orange slices\" width=\"1000\" height=\"667\" class=\"gu-image\" /> <figcaption> <span class=\"element-image__caption\">Claire Ptak\u2019s orange, ginger and rye upside-down cake.</span> <span class=\"element-image__credit\">Photograph: Kristin Perers/The Guardian</span> </figcaption> </figure>  <p>For now, berries, \u201cone of the most expensive fruits\u201d, are unlikely to come down in price and mangoes are well and truly gone.</p> <p>Keep the summer dream alive with good stone fruit \u2013 the last of the season \u2013 which to Thaker\u2019s surprise, are still good quality.</p> <p>\u201cUsually by this time, they\u2019re going black inside and rotting \u2026 I think customers should make the most of it.\u201d</p> <p><em><strong>Buy:</strong></em> <br>Apples<br>Asian greens<br>Bananas: stable year-round<br>Broccoli<br>Broccolini<br>Cauliflower<br>Cabbage<br>Corn<br>Eggplant<br>Fennel<br>Grapes<br>Green beans<br>Kale<br>Lemons<br>Lettuce<br>Limes<br>Pears<br>Silverbeet<br>Watermelon: rising in price, but still cheap<br>Wombok<br>Zucchini</p> <p><em><strong>Watch:</strong></em><br>Cucumbers: rising slightly in price<br>Persimmons: coming down in price<br>Pomegranates: coming into season <br>Stone fruit: at their end, so get in fast</p> <p><em><strong>Avoid:</strong></em> <br>Mangoes: gone<br>Tomatoes: expensive<br>Berries: expensive</p>", "bodyTextSummary": "April guarantees a plentiful supply of chocolate eggs, hot cross buns \u2026 and broccoli. There are plenty of fresh, affordable vegetables this month, and the green brassica stands out for all the right reasons. \u201c[Broccoli] is cheap, affordable and something that most families enjoy,\u201d says George Vasilevski, the owner of Yarraville Square Fresh Market in Melbourne. \u201cYou can find a rougher-grade broccoli, which doesn\u2019t look as pretty but is just as fresh, for as little as $2 a kilo but you shouldn\u2019t be paying more than $6 a kilo for the best.\u201d In supermarkets it can be found for about $4 a kilo.\nRoasting is one of the best ways to cook broccoli \u2013 the high heat gives a complex, nutty savouriness to the florets and stalks. With one large batch of roasted broccoli, the chef Alex Bluett has created four recipes: a salad, a blue-cheese gratin, a soup and a toastie. If you need to be broc-convinced, the vegetable goes (almost) incognito in Yotam Ottolenghi\u2019s orecchiette with broccoli and rocket. For the converted, Rachel Roddy\u2019s broccoli ripassati tossed through casarecce is the green pasta of choice.\nElsewhere in the brassica family, Vasilevski says there are plenty of bargain buys this month. Cauliflowers are back, and a steal at about $2.50 to $3 each. Get ahead with Felicity Cloake\u2019s guide to cooking the perfect whole-roasted cauliflower before spinning off with Nigel Slater\u2019s roasted cauliflower with lemon harissa sauce or Meera Sodha\u2019s cumin-and-chilli-spiced number with pilaf. And let this be the season for cauliflower tacos.\nKale is fresh and crisp at about $4.50 a bunch; a bunch of silverbeet will set you back about $5.50. Half savoy cabbages remain steady at about $3 each in supermarkets, while whole womboks can be found at $4.90 each and are destined for your next homemade kimchi. Keen for zucchinis April\u2019s zucchinis are gourd\u2019s gifts. Vasilevski calls them \u201cgreat value and very versatile\u201d and is selling them at $2 to $6 a kilo, depending on quality. In supermarkets, they are about $4.50 a kilo.\nMattie Taiano\u2019s zucchini lasagne is meat-free; Alice Zaslavsky\u2019s zucchini fritters are gluten-free, dairy-free, egg-free and nut-free; while Aleksandar Taralezhkov has created a zucchini multiverse with Bulgarian dolma, moussaka and koftas.\nAt the Greener Grocer in Maroubra in Sydney\u2019s east, its manager, Adam Balloot, says April is also the time to watch for grey zucchinis (often sold as Lebanese zucchinis). They are so named for their grey-coloured seeds and have a slightly sweeter flavour than green zucchinis. Red and green capsicums are abundant and can be found for $7 to $8 a kilo in supermarkets. Yellow capsicums, the sweetest of the lot, are about $12 to $13 a kilo. They\u2019re pricier because they have spent more time on the vine before harvesting. If your capsicums have spent a little too long lingering in the fridge, give them a second chance at life with Rachel Roddy\u2019s sweet and sour capsicum and potatoes.\nAlso in stable supply are Asian greens, eggplant, corn and fennel. After a late-summer glut, it\u2019s wise to leave tomatoes off your shopping list. \u201cAbout a month ago, we were selling 1kg bags for $2.50,\u201d Balloot says. \u201cToday, we have a 1kg bag for $4.\u201d In supermarkets, most varieties have risen to $7 or $8 a kilo for loose tomatoes. \u201cIf you can get your hands on a prepacked one, that\u2019s going to be a better deal right now,\u201d Balloot says. He says avocados are \u201cstill a bit iffy\u201d and, while prices are slowly going down each week, the much-loved Hass variety is not expected to return soon. Which means now is the time to embrace Shepards. The latter variety is good for baking into these cakes, tarts and apple crumble muffins.\n\u201cThe most popular are Pink Ladies, but they\u2019re one of the last apples to come in. Keep the summer dream alive with good stone fruit \u2013 the last of the season \u2013 which to Thaker\u2019s surprise, are still good quality. \u201cUsually by this time, they\u2019re going black inside and rotting \u2026 I think customers should make the most of it.\u201d Buy: Apples Asian greens Bananas: stable year-round Broccoli Broccolini Cauliflower Cabbage Corn Eggplant Fennel Grapes Green beans Kale Lemons Lettuce Limes Pears Silverbeet Watermelon: rising in price, but still cheap Wombok Zucchini Watch: Cucumbers: rising slightly in price Persimmons: coming down in price Pomegranates: coming into season Stone fruit: at their end, so get in fast Avoid: Mangoes: gone Tomatoes: expensive Berries: expensive", "attributes": {}, "published": true, "createdDate": "2023-04-04T00:00:31Z", "firstPublishedDate": "2023-04-04T00:00:31Z", "publishedDate": "2023-04-04T00:38:47Z", "lastModifiedDate": "2023-04-04T00:38:45Z", "contributors": [], "elements": [{"type": "text", "assets": [], "textTypeData": {"html": "<p>April guarantees a plentiful supply of chocolate eggs, hot cross buns \u2026 and broccoli.
